field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lesson is aimed to overcome low self-worth and help each student to understand that valuing other’s worth is equally important as their own self-worth. Students will learn and appreciate God’s view of a person’s worth (religion) and compare it to the modern view of a person’s worth (science). Using specific probing questions and diverse resources, students will be asked to evaluate and then reevaluate their own thoughts about self-worth and other human beings’ worth and how this impacts their everyday words and actions.<br /> </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p> </p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Each human being is born in the image and likeness of God - we are born with goodness; therefore, we all should strive our entire lifetime to make good choices.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Each student will gain the importance of how just one man’s viewpoint and actions can change the world, especially for the betterment of humankind. (MLK’s speech, including those who wrote and worked together (teamwork) to provide resources used in this lesson, etc.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="3"> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Each student will know that his/her own life is just as important as any other human being’s life in the world. In God’s view, money or power does not matter, so each will feel just as valued as any other person, regardless of wealth or status.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="4"> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Each student will know that self-respect is given to us from our birth by God. Because of this, we should live our lives everyday to uphold that self-respect and that respect from others is earned in how we treat one another everyday.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><p> </p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Describe a God view of self and a God view of humankind.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Identify erroneous views of self and humankind.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Show the relationship of a human being’s worth to each CST theme. i.e., The Life and Dignity of the Human Person, Solidarity, etc.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Share their knowledge of worthiness with others on an ongoing basis, including those closest to them and strangers.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong>Strive every day to show (in words and actions) the highest value of other’s worth and the highest value of one’s own self-worth. </strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>See for themselves how this worthiness (both other’s worth and self-worth) compliments each other and builds confidence and self-esteem. </span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p> </p> <p><strong><span><span><span><span><span><span>A. Timing - Three 50-minute lessons in the same week </span></span></span></span></span></span></strong></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Introduction (Day One) - 50 minutes, using the ClearTouch screen with discussion and the class bible</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Main Body (Day One and Day Two) - 50 minutes, using the ClearTouch screen with YouTube videos with discussion and the class bible</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Conclusion (Day Three) - 50 minutes, using ClearTouch Screen with YouTube videos and the class bible</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>B. Day One &amp; Day Two (Introduction and Main Body)</span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>INTRODUCTION: BELLINGER: </span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>What is a human being worth - modern view and God’s view? </span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>I will allow all students to answer this question in their own words at the very beginning of class. I will allow 5 minutes for the modern view and 5 minutes for God’s view. Then we’ll discuss as a class, and I will have student volunteers to board answers for each view.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>MAIN BODY:</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Will board these 2 questions on ClearTouch screen:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>(a) What does the “modern” view mean? </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>(b) What does “God’s” view mean? </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>I will divide the class into groups of 3-4 and have each group appoint a leader. To define the divine viewpoint (God’s), I will have students read aloud these biblical passages and write down their interpretations: (1) Genesis 1:25-27, Matthew 10: 29-31 and John 3:16 (2) “Man: The Image of God” (Catechism of the Catholic Church). To define the modern viewpoint, I will have students read aloud “The Christian Doctrine of Man” by Dr. Martin Luther King, Jr. and write down their interpretations. On my large ClearTouch screen, I will have student volunteers (other than the group leaders) to board answers from each group on the definitions of modern view and God’s view. At the end of day one class period, I will show the YouTube Video: “Human Worth &amp; a Look at Self-Worth and ask for student responses.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>C. Day Three (Conclusion)</span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>I will show 2 USCCB Catholic Social Teaching (CST) videos back-to-back. Before showing, I will let them know that all students are expected to share 3 specific phrases or observations from each video and how each is connected to the 2 CST Themes: </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>The Life and Dignity of the Human Person</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Solidarity</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Final Questions for this lesson: </span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>What is your own life worth? Is your life worth the same as any other human being in the world?</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> I will ask for the simplest answers possible from each student with the simplest explanations for each question. I will board the answers on the ClearTouch screen and then have students discuss their answers. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>I will end with a simple summary and reading aloud Psalm 139:14.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><em><strong>PRE-ASSESSMENT:</strong></em></p> <p><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>INTRODUCTION: BELLINGER: </span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>What is a human being worth - modern view and God’s view? </span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p>Answers to this question will enable me to collect information about what the students already know when they enter the classroom, and where they have gaps in their knowledge. With this information, I can help students build on what they already know.</p> <p> </p> <p><em><strong>FORMATIVE ASSESSMENT: </strong></em></p> <p><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span><span><span>MAIN BODY:</span></span></span></span></strong></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> <strong>Will board these 2 questions on ClearTouch screen:</strong></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><strong><span><span><span><span><span><span>(a) What does the “modern” view mean? </span></span></span></span></span></span></strong></p> <p><strong><span><span><span><span><span><span>(b) What does “God’s” view mean? </span></span></span></span></span></span></strong></p> <p>These tools (probing questions, diverse resources - Catechism of the Catholic Church/MLK's doctrines, bible passages, YouTube videos, etc, and collaboration with teachers and classmates) identify misconceptions, struggles, and learning gaps along the way and assess how to close those gaps. Effective tools help to shape learning and can even bolster students’ abilities to take ownership of their learning when they understand that the goal is to improve learning.</p> <p> </p> <p><em><strong>SUMMATIVE ASSESSMENT:</strong></em></p> <p><span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>CONCLUSION: Final Questions for this lesson: </span></span></strong></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>What is your own life worth? Is your life worth the same as any other human being in the world? </span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p>Summative assessments evaluate student learning, knowledge, proficiency, or success at the conclusion of an instructional period or lesson. Students' answers to these questions will assist me in evaluating if the goals of the lesson were accomplished. If not, I am able to adjust/change the lesson for maximum efficacy in the future.</p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' world place upon a human being?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What worth does God place upon a human being?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>How do you view your own worth?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>1.  </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Identify living and non-living things. Articulate the difference between them.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>2. </span></span></strong><span><span>State Aristotle's four causes and relate them to living and non-living things.</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>3. </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Compare and contrast the characteristics of plants, animals, and humans as living things</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>4. </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Demonstrate understanding of Aquinas’ faculties/powers of the human soul</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>5. </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Relate Aquinas’ faculties of the human to the characteristics of living things. Identify which powers are common to plants, animals, and humans. Which are found only in humans?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><strong>6</strong>. Identify and define the philosophical worldview of  scientific materialism </span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>(</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>material world is all that exists)</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Identify and define the Catholic Christian philosophical worldview. Explain how these world views affect how we view living things.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * What makes something a living thing? What is the animating principle of a living thing?</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>2. How do the biologist's “characteristics of living things” relate to Aquinas’s faculties/powers of the human soul?</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>3. Do other animals have all of the same faculties/powers of the soul as humans? Which ones do they have and which ones don’t they have? What about a plant?</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>4. How does Scientific Materialism (material world is all that exists) affect the view of living things as living?</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT Modern science and church doctrine had to develop an ordered process to help uncover the truth. </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span>1. Compare the processes used to find answers in science and religion</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span>2. Understand a literal and literalist reading of the Bible</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span>3. Explain that the Catholic Faith is a faith of reason</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span>4. </span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span>The ability to recognize credible sources of information</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Design and carry out an experiment using the scientific method.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Compare and contrast creation accounts in the Bible.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Analyzing and interpreting data</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Obtain, evaluate, and communicate information</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Evaluation based on developing a claim, backing up with evidence, and develop an explanation. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><strong>Investigative Phenomena</strong>: Use JamBoard to present the following question, (come up with a question that will allow students to answer the question without any research, showing me what they already know.  This will give every student a voice and will allow students to go back to possibly revise their own thinking/model) </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Have you believed a misconception or misunderstood a concept? How did you “fix” the misconception or misunderstanding?</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Run an experiment that will use the scientific method. </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span> Can the flavor of candy influence the amount of bacteria found in our mouth? </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Conclusion: Make sure to emphasize the comparison of the data.  Is the hypothesis supported by the data? Should you speak with other “scientists” in your class to discuss their procedure and results? Would you be willing to recommend a candy flavor citing the fact that it WILL decrease bacteria in your mouth?  Would you be willing to publish your data and stand behind your conclusion without any reservations? If not, what would need to happen with this experiment? To create a set of data, that would be scientifically reliable and accurate? What process do scientists go through to publish their work?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Create a class investigation and discussion comparing the Creation account in Genesis 1 with different creation accounts found in the Bible.  See the list of the other creation accounts. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Divide students into groups of 4.  Hand each group the creation story from Genesis 1 and have students read aloud together.  On the board ask each group to answer the following questions: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>What do you notice?  What do you wonder?</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Choose 4 other creation accounts from the Bible. Groups may receive all of the same additional creation accounts or groups can be given different creation accounts.  On the board ask each group to answer the following questions: </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>What do you notice?  What do you wonder?</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Discuss the terms literal and literalism.  Give some examples: “raining cats and dogs”  “I slept like a baby”   </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Have students compare the Genesis 1 account of creation and let groups choose another creation account from the 4 that were handed out.  Have students compare and contrast the account.  </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Ask each group to share their findings.  This can be done in a variety of formats.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Based on the different accounts of creation in the Bible, was there just one account used to guide our understanding of creation?  How do you think scholars/theologians use these accounts to uncover the truth of creation? How do you uncover truth when there are different accounts you have been told, for example you leave out your hot fudge sundae and when you come back it has been eaten?</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>How is the creation account in the Bible different from the scientific account of creation?  Do you think there are any misconceptions or misunderstandings?  How do you think the Catholic Church makes a determination regarding (science topics?)  </span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Have student research resources </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://inters.org/anthology-and-documents"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://inters.org/anthology-and-documents</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> found on this website that demonstrate a variety of ways the Church has uncovered the truth. Have groups share their findings with the class.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span>C.E.R.  </span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span>As an ecologist you have been tasked to present to a group of teachers about Laudato Si.  In your presentation you must discuss why ecological diversity is important and how the Catholic Church asks us to be good stewards of our common home to protect ecological diversity. </span></span></span></span></span></p> <p>Make a claim as to the value of biodiversity which is supported by the teachings of the Catholic Church. Use evidence from the natural world and religious realm. Write a scientific explanation to justify your claim.<br />  </p> <p>Claim:</p> <p>Evidence:</p> <p>Reasoning:</p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-standards--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-standards.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-standards.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-standards field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>NGSS Science and Engineering Practices</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1.</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Asking Questions and Defining Problems</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">2-3 45min class periods to discuss and experiment with the notion of mystery in science. It includes personal reflection, small and large group discussion followed by two simple activities involving properties of light. The lesson includes formative observational and written assessments as well as a brief summative comprehension assignment. </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN">Knowledge:</span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN">1. Modern physics describes light as having properties of both waves and particles, not one or the other. </span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN">2. The current description of light is an example of a mystery in science. </span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN">3. Science uses a process to arrive at deeper understanding of physical phenomena. </span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN">4. Science contains elements of ‘mystery’ or unknown concepts in need of further study and imagination.</span></span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN">Demonstrate and explain how light acts as particle using the “magic bending straw” lab.</span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN">Explain how light has the properties of a wave utilizing the diffraction grating and laser demonstration. </span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN">Communicate understanding of the mystery of light as both particle and wave through discussion and written expression. </span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN">Evaluate additional scientific inquiries for aspects of mystery. </span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span>1. Diagnostic Survey (individual 5min jot down notes)</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span>guiding ?s (reveal 1 question at a time to students)</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span>          a. What is mystery? --- are there different types?</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span>          b. Can you identify any mysteries in scientific fields? </span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span>          c. What is similar/different about these mysteries?</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span>2. Small Group w/their notes – share/discuss/&amp; focus on 1-2 key insights</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span>3. Large Group share/discuss guiding ?s</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span>4. (HW or within first 45min) – Reflect: Summarize your understanding of mystery and explain how it may have changed from this discussion (1-2 paragraphs)</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span>5. (start of class 2) – mini lab/thought exercises with shadows and straw in water glass.  </span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span>6. Quick demo: What do you expect to see when shining a laser through 2 holes? wave demo (or show video of)  </span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span>7. lecture/discussion elaborating how light <em>mysteriously </em>is both light and particle – address conception/misconception of mystery.</span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN"><span>8. Comprehension quiz (HW or class session 3)</span></span></span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span lang="EN" xml:lang="EN" xml:lang="EN">1. field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lecture looks to guide the students through a Socratic seminar to explore definitions of faith and reason, and then to help them begin to understand how those need each other. This lecture will utilize a series of questions to draw the students in and encourage them to seek the answers on their own, guided by the teacher. High School 11th-12th grade. </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span>Articulate definitions of faith and reason as understood by the Catholic Church.</span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span>Articulate several examples of where science requires the use of faith. </span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span>Compare and contrast the use of reason as it relates to science as well as our belief in Christ.</span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span>Describe an example in the study of science for which faith contributed to a more complete understanding of the science or vice versa.</span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span>Know the definition of truth - and how it relates to faith and reason.</span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span>Know that theology is the queen of the sciences.</span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Capable of articulating how religion and science both require the use of faith and reason</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Integrates understanding of ideas which are usually seen as contradictory, using both faith and science to come to the truth.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Assesses a claim based on the use of clearly defined terms and evidence</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Know how to assess the truth of a claim and when it is not possible to know the reality of the situation.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Timing: </span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>One 90 minute class period</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>As we begin all things, we begin with prayer.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Opening question: What is faith? Definition of terms discussion</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>As an opener, we ask students to share their initial impressions of the term and what it means to them.  Expected answers would include those making mention of religion or deeply held personal beliefs.  The goal here is to get a sense of what understanding they come into the class with.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Follow up question: Can you give an example of when you believed something on the word of another?  Give examples.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Expected answers include…?</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>I have a pancreas.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Botswana is a country in Africa. (Assuming no one in class has been there)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Atoms have electrons.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Birds are real. (Are they?)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>The mitochondria is the powerhouse of the cell.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Now we define faith: holding something as true on the basis of the account of another.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>We distinguish between natural and supernatural faith.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Natural is based on the word of another person.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Supernatural is based on Divine Revelation</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Based on the above answers to the follow up question, ask students if they are being rational to believe these things on faith? Or are they being irrational by believing them?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Transition question: What is reason? What does it mean to be rational?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>We must define reason: So, what do we mean by rational?  Expected answers:</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Once again we ask students to share their initial impressions of the term and go from there. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Logical</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Demonstrable</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>In accordance with reality</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is science: Usually we mean the study of the material world using the scientific method.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Perhaps explore what else science has meant as “knowledge” (Theology = Sacred Science)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students should be able to explain what is meant by the scientific method…</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Follow up question: when would you say it is rational to believe someone else?</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Is faith reasonable?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Questions and criteria for belief:</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Is the source trustworthy?  </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Does what is being said make sense?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Is there any evidence or logical arguments to support what is said?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>For example: it is rational to believe my mechanic about the diagnosis about my car, because he is an expert on the topic, and can point to symptoms observed in the car’s operation.  On the other hand, believing my mechanic about his claims that there is extraterrestrial intelligent life makes less sense: he has little knowledge of that subject, and even less in the way of evidence.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>[Insert examples of news stories or claims and have the class determine whether they are reasonable; perhaps slip a </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Babylon Bee</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> story in there.]</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Follow up question:  Can you study science without faith?  Do scientists rely on the assertions of others to do their work?  Of course they do!  Discovery builds on discovery.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Give examples of a scientific discovery that resulted from assuming the accuracy of a previous discovery or law.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Science then, an exercise of human reason about the material world, does not exclude, and, in fact, practically uses, natural faith.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Returning to a question of supernatural faith: is our belief in divine revelation rational?  Let us explore:</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Is the source trustworthy?  What do we understand the source of Divine Revelation to be?</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> God.</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>How do we know this?  Here we could discuss the witness of the Apostles, etc.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Does what is being said make sense?</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>It does, although it can transcend reason in cases of mystery.  A mystery being a truth that goes beyond human understanding.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Is there any evidence or logical arguments to support what is said?</span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>We have the witness of the Apostles, martyrs; we have the explanations of the Doctors of the Church; we have the example of the miraculous.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>This only begins the discussion.  The key here: faith is not contrary to reason, but it is actually needed to exercise it!  Our supernatural/theological faith, then, while transcending reason and demanding real faith, is not contrary to reason.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p>Exit Ticket: In light of our conversation, and in your own words, answer the following questions. Use complete sentences and number the questions and answers on a clean sheet of paper.</p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. What is faith? Is faith necessary for scientific inquiry? </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. What is reason? Is reason necessary for religion?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Is faith reasonable?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>4.In what ways have we used both faith and reason as part of our learning process? In the ways we have used faith, is that reasonable faith?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * class="field field--name-field-lesson-resources field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Lesson Resources</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>“What’s the Deal with Birds,” </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="http://www.chm.bris.ac.uk/sillymolecules/birds.pdf"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>http://www.chm.bris.ac.uk/sillymolecules/birds.pdf</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>"</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span>Science Confirms Sounds Of Dad’s Bodily Functions Increase By 30 Decibels Every Year Of Life"   <span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://babylonbee.com/news/science-confirms-dads-bodily-functions-increase-by-30-decibels-every-year-of-life</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span> <ul> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>NOTE:</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> The two above sources are to be used as a legitimate looking sources that are in fact satirical!</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>“Fides et Ratio,” </span></span></span></span></span></span><a field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lesson explores a future potential use of the Crispr-Cas9 technique to create designer babies. Students will be asked to order a child and then examine the consequences of commodifying the creation of human life. There is an order form, a presentation, and suggested role playing ideas. Student groups can be assigned different amounts of money to spend on the design of their child.<br /> <br /> We recognize the responsibilities given to us by God concerning the human condition; through technology, we have the capacity to alter and commodify human life. At this point in our history, we cannot afford to reduce life merely to its constituent components but need to utilize both science and religion in order to inform a moral as well as a material understanding of man. In doing so we need to come to a clear understanding of who the man is, his dignity, and his purpose. It is in this way we seek to join the insights of faith and science in order to produce a more complete view of what it means to be human.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * we currently have the potential technology (Crispr/Cas 9 with </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>in vitro </span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>fertilization) to greatly influence what it means to be human (we are now a field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><h2><span><span><span><span><span><span>(Recommended Formative)</span></span></span></span></span></span></h2> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Role play - students will be divided into 3 person groups and roleplay three different scenarios.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Scenario 1: ( Discussion of commodification)</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Roles:  Mom, Dad and Ordered Child</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Guided/suggested questions:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>For what purpose would mom and dad choose gene editing? Justify their choices.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Why don’t I look like you?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>How does the ordered child feel about being “designed”? </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What is my value?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p> </p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Session 2 ( Discussion on familial effects.)</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Roles: Grandparent, Ordered Child, Ordered Child’s Child</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Guided/suggested questions:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>As an ordered child, would you want to design your child as well, why or why not?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Given the genetic change within the ordered child and the birth of their child what effect does this have on the relationship with the grandparents and family dynamics (traditions, gatherings,...)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p> </p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Session 3 ( Socioeconomic outcomes)</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Roles: Ordered Child, Classmate who is Naturally Born, Classmate who is an Ordered Child of a Wealthier Couple </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>What will be the possible socioeconomic outcomes( class, education, occupations etc.)  within the family and society between, natural-born children, designed (ordered) children of a middle class family and, the designed (ordered) children of a wealthy family?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <drupal-render-placeholder <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will compare and contrast Newton’s views of the Trinity and the Catechism view of the Trinity.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will demonstrate a basic understanding of reductionism.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="3"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will understand God is a being outside of the universe.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="4"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will describe the basic method error Newton made in analyzing scripture.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Synthesize a conclusion after reading multiple academic sources</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Describe the appropriate use of reductionism</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Describe the Mystery of the Trinity in light of the Catechism</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Introduction / Ice Breaker</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will describe a parent as best they are able.  They will then analyze their descriptions and sort their comments into two categories, either physical or non-physical.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will consider the question - is there more to the person you described than their physical characteristics?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Part I</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will read the Baglow textbook “Faith, Science and Reason” p47-51 about Newton’s flaws. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will compare Newton’s view of God’s relationship to the universe to the Catholic view of God’s relationship to the universe.  For example, compare how Newton views gravitational forces between masses and how the Church would view the origin of gravitational forces between masses.  Students should conclude that Newton sees God as within the universe acting to push masses toward each other.  In contrast, the Church sees God as transcendent to the universe and masses attract each other because the masses are obeying physical law God wrote prescribing how masses will act on each other..  </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Part II</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will read the excerpts from the talk entitled “Newton - Rationalizing Christianity or Not?”  by Rosalind Picard from MIT about Newton’s views of Christianity.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will read the excerpts from the Catechism on the Doctrine of the Trinity.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will view a short discussion of the Trinity entitled “What is the Trinity” </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>by Bishop Robert Barron -</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ToOHfdixzok</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will compare Newton’s views of the divine nature of Jesus to the Church’s view about the divine nature of Jesus.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will compare Newton’s views on the Mystery of the Trinity and the Catechism statements on the Mystery of the Trinity.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Conclusion - Final Discussion</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will consider these questions during a discussion of the readings::</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ul> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Why does Newton think the book of nature and the book of scripture should agree on all things?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Why does Newton think human reason, over the centuries,  has corrupted what scripture says?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Why does Newton wish to reduce what scripture says about the Trinity, directly or indirectly, to what is in his mind immediately apparent in the text of scripture?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ul> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: *
