field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Pre-test on Isaac Newton  (this pre assessment could be given before or just after the ice breaker)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will respond on a five point scale (strongly disagree to strongly  agree)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Isaac Newton accepted Jesus as the divine Son of God.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Isaac Newton accepted the Mystery of the Trinity.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Isaac Newton was troubled by two bodies separated in space attracting each other.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Isaac Newton thought God directly intervened in the universe to cause two separated bodies to attract each other. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> Issac Newton thought Sacred Scripture should be read literally.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><br /> <br /> <br />  </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Post-Quiz on Isaac Newton (this will be given after students have finished all parts of the lesson on Newton and Faith and Reason)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> T or F  Isaac Newton thought Sacred Scripture must be interpreted as plainly as </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>             possible.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> T or F  Issac Newton read Sacred Scripture to imply that Jesus was subservient to the</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>             Father and did not not share fully in the Father’s divine nature.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="3"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> T or F  Issac Newton thought Sacred Scripture and what a scientific study of the </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>             universe revealed about God would have differences.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="4"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>T or F  Human reason alone is capable of understanding the full meaning of</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>            the Holy Trinity.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="5"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>T or F  The Holy Trinity is more apparent after Jesus sends the Holy Spirit to the </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>            Apostles.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="6"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>T or F  The Holy Trinity is a union of three divine persons through divine love.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="7"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>T or F  Isaac Newton understood his mathematical description of gravity did not fully </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>            describe what the nature of gravity is.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="8"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>T or F   In science, reducing a larger set of rules for a system to a smaller yet </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>             equivalently descriptive set of rules, shows a better understanding of the </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>             system.   </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="9"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>T or F  The Catechism if the Church maintains some knowledge of God must be directly </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>            revealed to us.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="10"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> T or F  Isaac Newton thought he was rediscovering the true meaning of Sacred </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>             Scripture as he analyzed it and rejected the Trinity and the divine nature of </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>             Jesus.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Subjective Assessment- </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Writing Prompt  (students will respond in about 150-250 words to this prompt)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Newton reduced Kepler’s laws of planetary motion to his universal law of gravitation and his laws of motion.  His laws were more fundamental and powerful in that they could predict the motion of all masses, not just the planets in the solar system.  Newton used this reduction strategy in analyzing Sacred Scripture as well.  He thought Sacred Scripture should be read as plainly as possible.  Thinking about the Trinity, we recall that Mysteries of the Catholic faith are hidden in God and can never be known unless they are revealed by God.  The mystery of the Most Holy Trinity is the central mystery of Christian faith and life. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><em><span>Write a few paragraphs explaining why Newton is making a mistake in the way he is analyzing Sacred Scripture and in the way he analyzed the doctrine of the Trinity.  Explain at least in an elementary way, the Doctrine of the Trinity.</span></em></span></span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <drupal-render-placeholder callback="flag.link_builder:build" arguments="0=node&amp;1=274&amp;2=favorite_lessons" token="YCRWM3u51nG0AtKA19q5fegrzzy2WLPNzpR-jN-TYx4"></drupal-render-placeholder> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-resources--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-resources.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-resources.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-resources field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Lesson Resources</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will read p. 47-50 from the Baglow textbook “Faith, Science, and Reason”.  The specific  section in the textbook is “Newton’s Laws and Newton’s Flaws”.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p> </p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will read these excerpts from a talk entitled, “Newton - Rationalizing Christianity - or not?” by Rosalind Picard.  (see below for the excepts)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><br /> <br /> <br />  </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>From Picard-</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Newton bound religion and science in many ways, believing that whatever knowledge of God was revealed in ``the Book of Nature'' was harmonious with what was unfolded in ``the Book of Scripture.'' Newton thought that science had nothing to say about the dogmatic content of religion, and that Scripture was not to be quoted in a Royal Society communication (Manuel, 1974, p. 48), but these were small separations compared with his faith that God's work was behind both ``Books.''</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>``A quest for simplicity and unity'' underlay Newton's research into both the Book of God and the Book of Nature. (Manuel, 1974, pp. 48-49). Here is what Newton wrote in one of his reflections in a manuscript on rules for interpreting prophecy:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>``Truth is ever to be found in simplicity, and not in the multiplicity and confusion of things. As the world, which to the naked eye exhibits the greatest variety of objects, appears very simple in its internal constitution when surveyed by a philosophic understanding, and so much the simpler by how much the better it is understood, so it is in these [prophetic] visions. It is the perfection of God's works that they are all done with the greatest simplicity. He is the God of order and not of confusion. And therefore as they that would understand the frame of the world must endeavor to reduce their knowledge to all possible simplicity, so it must be in seeking to understand these visions.''</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Manuel (1974) points out that Newton, instead of trying to highlight differences, highlighted a divine simplicity that permeates Nature and Scripture, as would befit the works of one Master Creator.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Newton's Christ was ``the Christ of unadorned scripture, the Christ whom God revealed to men, not the Christ of reason'' (Davis, 1991). Newton, commenting on the scripture 2 Tim 1:13, "Hold fast to the form of sound words,.." indicated that it was not sufficient that a component of one's faith could be deduced from scripture, but said, ``It must be expressed in the very form of sound words in which it was delivered by the Apostles,'' for men were apt to ``run into partings about deductions. All the old Heresies lay in deductions; the true faith was in the text'' (Manuel 1974 pp. 54-55). </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Let me recite several findings from (Manuel 1974, pp 57-61). Here we learn that Newton went to a lot of trouble to distinguish his private beliefs about the nature of Christ from the beliefs of both orthodox Trinitarians and those who believed Christ had been a mere man. Regarding the trinity, Newton contended that the name God was never used in Scripture to denote more than one of the three persons of the Trinity at the same time, and that when it appeared without particular reference to the Son or the Holy Ghost, it always signified the Father. Newton argued that the distinction of the Son from the Father was further evidenced by the Son's confession of His dependence upon the will of the Father, by His acknowledgment that the Father was greater, and that prescience of all future things was in the Father alone. ``But Christ was not a mere man,'' Manuel continues. ``He was the Son of God, not just a human soul who was sent into the world... Though this did not limit the power of the Son, it meant that Christ's power was derived from the Father and that of Himself He could do nothing. In all things the Son submitted His will to the Father, which would altogether be unreasonable if He were His equal. The union of Father and Son was ... an agreement of wills. The same attributes could be applied to the Father and to the Son, but they were different in nature since the Son's attributes were a grant from the Father.'' In Newton's words:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>``The heathens made all their Gods of one substance and sometimes called them one God, and yet were polytheists. Nothing can make two persons one God but unity of dominion. And if the Father and Son be united in dominion, the son being subordinate to the father and sitting in his throne, they can no more be called two Gods then a King and his viceroy can be called two kings.'' Newton refuted the doctrine of consubstantiality, arguing that it did not establish Christ's divinity or his right to be adored -- ``The heathens and Gnosticks supposed not only their Gods but even the souls of men and the starrs to be of one substance with the supreme God and yet were Idolaters for worshipping them.....Tis not consubstantiality but power and dominion which gives a right to be worshipped.'' (Manuel 1974, pp 59-60).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Students will view the short talk on the Trinity entitled “What is the Trinity”.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Link for the video is: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ToOHfdixzok</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Students will also read these excerpts from the Catechism of the Catholic Church on the Trinity:</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><br /> <br />  </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>CATECHISM OF THE CATHOLIC CHURCH</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>SECOND EDITION</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>237</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> The Trinity is a mystery of faith in the strict sense, one of the "mysteries that are hidden in God, which can never be known unless they are revealed by God".</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><sup>58</sup></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> To be sure, God has left traces of his Trinitarian being in his work of creation and in his Revelation throughout the Old Testament. But his inmost Being as Holy Trinity is a mystery that is inaccessible to reason alone or even to Israel's faith before the Incarnation of God's Son and the sending of the Holy Spirit. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>234</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> The mystery of the Most Holy Trinity is the central mystery of Christian faith and life. It is the mystery of God in himself. It is therefore the source of all the other mysteries of faith, the light that enlightens them. It is the most fundamental and essential teaching in the "hierarchy of the truths of faith".</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><sup>56</sup></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> The whole history of salvation is identical with the history of the way and the means by which the one true God, Father, Son and Holy Spirit, reveals himself to men "and reconciles and unites with himself those who turn away from sin".</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><sup>57</sup></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>The dogma of the Holy Trinity</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>253</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>The Trinity is One</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>. We do not confess three Gods, but one God in three persons, the "consubstantial Trinity".</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><sup>83</sup></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> The divine persons do not share the one divinity among themselves but each of them is God whole and entire: "The Father is that which the Son is, the Son that which the Father is, the Father and the Son that which the Holy Spirit is, i.e. by nature one God."</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><sup>84</sup></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> In the words of the Fourth Lateran Council (1215), "Each of the persons is that supreme reality, viz., the divine substance, essence or nature."</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><sup>85</sup></span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>254</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>The divine persons are really distinct from one another</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>. "God is one but not solitary."</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><sup>86</sup></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> "Father", "Son", "Holy Spirit" are not simply names designating modalities of the divine being, for they are really distinct from one another: "He is not the Father who is the Son, nor is the Son he who is the Father, nor is the Holy Spirit he who is the Father or the Son."</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><sup>87</sup></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> They are distinct from one another in their relations of origin: "It is the Father who generates, the Son who is begotten, and the Holy Spirit who proceeds."</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><sup>88</sup></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> The divine Unity is Triune.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>255</span></span></strong></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>The divine persons are relative to one another</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>. Because it does not divide the divine unity, the real distinction of the persons from one another resides solely in the relationships which relate them to one another: "In the relational names of the persons the Father is related to the Son, the Son to the Father, and the Holy Spirit to both. While they are called three persons in view of their relations, we believe in one nature or substance."</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><sup>89</sup></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Indeed "everything (in them) is one where there is no opposition of relationship."</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><sup>90</sup></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> "Because of that unity the Father is wholly in the Son and wholly in the Holy Spirit; the Son is wholly in the Father and wholly in the Holy Spirit; the Holy Spirit is wholly in the Father and wholly in the Son."</span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span><sup>9</sup></span></span></span></span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Essential Questions</h4> <div class="field__item"><p> </p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Newton considered God as part of the universe.  What problems did this cause Newton when he thought about the origin of the universe and the origin of gravitational forces?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Newton thought that human reason applied to Sacred Scripture always corrupted the meaning of Scripture.  How did this lead Newton to reject the divine nature of Jesus and also reject the Mystery of the Trinity?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span> The Mystery of the Trinity involves love and relationship.  How does this perspective lead the Catechism to propose a reason for God to create the universe?</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lesson is aimed to help students understand the complementary nature of human creation and human evolution by using the modern popular culture reference of the 2016 movie Dr. Strange. At the end of this lesson, students will be able not only to explain the nature and faith and science with respect to the human being, but will also be able to analyze popular culture references with respect to their accuracy in portraying the relationship between faith and science. This lesson is ideally suited for religion classes that focus on Scripture or Faith and Science, but could also be used as a supplementary lesson to a biology class on evolution.</div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Describe God’s creation of humans in Genesis 2:7</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Differentiate natural selection (mechanism) from evolution (results of natural selection)</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Articulate how a proper reading of Genesis 2 shows that it compliments rather than conflicts with the Theory of Human Evolution</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Compare the scene in Dr. Strange with our understanding of how faith and science complement each other (</span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://youtu.be/TiRFUYfqr4E"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://youtu.be/TiRFUYfqr4E</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>) </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-skills--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-skills.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-skills.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Evaluate why we need both faith and science for our understanding of human creation/evolution</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Propose and explain another pop culture reference that can help us understand the relationship between the topic of Creator God and human evolution</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Analyze a pop culture reference that shows the conflict between faith and science and analyze the flaws in the root of the conflict</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Create an explanation as to why we need both faith and science for our complete understanding of human creation and human evolution</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-method--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-method.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-method.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-method field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Method</h4> <div class="field__item"><ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson Timing</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>A. 3-4 class days</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>B. One class day is 60-65 minutes</span></span></span></span></span></span><br />  </p> <ol start="2"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson Plan Structure: DAY 1 (Human Creation in Genesis 2)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>A. Quick survey about student views of a possible conflict between evolution and Catholicism. (Distribute document in RESOURCES, could be transformed into a Google Form, Quizlet, Survey Monkey, Socrative, etc)- approximately 5 minutes </span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>*Optional- show the class the results of the survey</span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>B. Discussion “Can you accept the Theory of Evolution and still be a Catholic?”- approximately 10-15 minutes</span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>C. Read Genesis 2:4-25; have students read by themselves first and then have the class as a whole read it aloud together. (RESOURCE- Bible)- approximately 10 minutes</span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>D. In small groups, have students make a list of observations they made from the reading. Then come back together as a large group and share their findings; the teacher should not respond to questions yet so that students can personally work through questions. Approximately 15 minutes</span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>E. Use Christopher Baglow’s </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Creation</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> pages 70-71 (RESOURCE) to discuss the historical background of Genesis 2. Last 15 minutes</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>F. HOMEWORK/ASSESSMENT (formative):  How does learning the historical context of Genesis 2 impact the way you understand it? In your response, touch upon what it is that you actually understand about Genesis 2. Minimum 5 complete sentences. </span></span></span></span></span></span><br />  </p> <ol start="3"> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson Plan Structure: DAY 2 (Human Evolution)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>A. Ask students to share any insights they made on the previous night’s assessment. To conclude this brief discussion, make sure to point out: humans are intentionally made for a purpose; creation is good; humans were given a task to care for the Earth; there is one God who is not in competition with others; all humans come from the same earth and gained their spirit from the one God. Approximately 5-10 minutes </span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>B. Brief Lecture: Who was Darwin, what are his tenants of natural selection, evolution as the result of natural selection (RESOURCE- textbook </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Faith, Science, &amp; Reason; Theology on the Cutting Edge</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span> Chapter 8, section B)- Approximately 20 minutes</span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>C. RESOURCE: Watch “Biological Evolution and the Kinship of All Life” (</span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://sciencereligiondialogue.org/resources/biological-evolution-and-the-kinship-of-all-life-2/"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://sciencereligiondialogue.org/resources/biological-evolution-and-the-kinship-of-all-life-2/</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>)  (round to 10 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>D. In a large group discussion, call on 3-4 students to share a thought about the video; transition to human evolution as the focus (approximately 5 minutes) </span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>E. Students should have access to a mobile device (iPad, Chromebook, computer, cell phone, etc) and go to </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://humanorigins.si.edu/"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://humanorigins.si.edu/</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span>. Go to: Human Evolution Evidence, then Human Fossils, then Species. For approximately 10 minutes, should should observe similarities and differences between the species on this website. Students should note physical traits in the skull such as shape of the skull, eyes, ears, presence of hair, etc. During the last 5 minutes, have students discuss as a class these similarities and differences, finishing with the primary difference between </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Homo sapiens </span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>and other species is the presence of the soul and rational thinking. </span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>F. HOMEWORK/ASSESSMENT (formative): RESOURCE (textbook) on page 235, question 1: “Watch the video ‘To Be Human’ mtfresources.org. Relate the video to the picture of human origins given in Genesis 2:7”- minimum of 5 complete, well-thought out sentences. </span></span></span></span></span></span><br />  </li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>Lesson Plan Structure: DAY 3-4 if needed (Pop Culture Connections)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>A. Begin class by distributing white paper to each student; using their homework from the night before, students should be instructed to create a visual interpretation of their written homework. Drawing should take 10-15 minutes with 5 minutes to discuss. </span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>*Option for the teacher to extend this upwards of 30 minutes, depending on how much the students would like to share. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>B. Transition into how we can see these connections in modern popular culture. Begin by showing the following clip from the 2016 movie </span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><em><span>Dr. Strange</span></em></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: </span></span></span></span></span></span><a href="https://youtu.be/TiRFUYfqr4E"><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>https://youtu.be/TiRFUYfqr4E</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></a><span><span><span><span><span><span> (5 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><br /> <br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>C. In half of the small groups, students should discuss the analogy of the various ways of perceiving a human with respect to how it connects to human creation and human evolution. </span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>The other half of the small groups should discuss if you agree/disagree with the following quote from the clip and why: "I reject it because I do not believe in fairy tales...there is no such thing as spirit!  We are made of matter and nothing more.  You are just another tiny, momentary speck within an indifferent universe" (10-15 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>D.  Come back together as a large group to first share thoughts and insights from the small group discussion. Be sure to mention the point that in this pop culture reference (leaving aside the chakra reference, but including the scientific images), it shows many pictures that discuss the same human but answer different questions. (10 minutes)</span></span></span></span></span></span><br /> <br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>E. Share the following information with the students BEFORE the large group discussion (RESOURCE: Baglow, “Faith, Reason and Science: Theology on the Cutting Edge” 2nd edition, pages 193-194):  The Catholic church has never condemned the theory of evolution.  Quotes to support this (5 minutes):</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>a.  “This is the gist of the theory of evolution as a scientific hypothesis. It is in perfect agreement with the Christian conception of the universe.”  -Catholic Encyclopedia, 1909</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>b. “Mr. Darwin’s theory need not be atheistical, be it true or not; it may simply be suggesting a large idea of Divine Prescience and Skill” –Cardinal John Henry Newman, 1868</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>c.“The Bible is not a textbook of science, and, therefore, cannot rightly be quoted either for or against evolution.” – “The Question Box”, a Catholic answers book, 1929</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>F. Discuss as a large group - how do Genesis 2 and Evolution offer 2 complementary </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>perspectives about what it means to be human? (Until the end of class, add more time </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>as needed)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Be sure to make the following points:</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <ol> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Genesis 2 is not a scientific text but a symbolic one</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>Both evolution and Scripture discuss the same humans but answer different questions. </span></span></span></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><span><span><span>A Catholic perspective on evolution reminds us that science can never prove/disprove the existence of the human soul, which is spiritual and given to us directly by God.</span></span></span></span></span></span></li> </ol> <p><br /> <span><span><span><span><span><span>G. HOMEWORK/ASSESSMENT (summative): Propose and explain another pop culture reference that can help us understand the relationship between the topic of Creator God and human evolution– students should be given a week (approximately) </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-assessment--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-assessment.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-assessment field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Assessment</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 1 HOMEWORK/ASSESSMENT:  How does learning the historical context of Genesis 2 impact the way you understand it? In your response, touch upon what it is that you actually understand about Genesis 2. Minimum 5 complete sentences. Grading Rubric in the RESOURCE section. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 2 HOMEWORK/ASSESSMENT: RESOURCE (textbook) on page 235, question 1: “Watch the video ‘To Be Human’ mtfresources.org. Relate the video to the picture of human origins given in Genesis 2:7” Grading Rubric in the RESOURCE section. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Day 3/ Extended Time Assignment HOMEWORK/ASSESSMENT: Propose and explain another pop culture reference that can help us understand the relationship between the topic of Creator God and human evolution– students should be given a week (approximately) Grading Rubric in the RESOURCE section. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-standards--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-standards.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-standards.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-standards field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Standards</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>USCCB</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Core Curriculum: </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. The Revelation of Jesus Christ in Scripture</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>II. About Sacred Scripture</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>A. Divine Inspiration.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. Inspiration is the gift of the Holy Spirit by which a human author was </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>able to write a biblical book which really has God as the author and which </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>teaches faithfully and without error the saving truth that God willed to be </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>consigned to us for our salvation (CCC, nos. 105, 135).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. Since God inspired the biblical writers, he is the author of Scripture </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>(CCC, nos. 105-106, 136).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Because the human authors needed to use the language and thinking </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>of their time, we need to study the conditions and use of language in the </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>context of their time and understand what they intended to communicate, </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>remembering that these human authors might not have been conscious of </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>the deeper implications of what God wanted to communicate (CCC, nos. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>106, 108-114).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>4. The Bible is inerrant in matters of Revelation and faith: because God is </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>the author of Scripture, all the religious truths that God intends to reveal </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>concerning our salvation are true; this attribute is called “inerrancy” (see </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>DV, no. 11; CCC, no. 107).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>III. Understanding Scripture</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>B. Criteria for interpreting the Sacred Scripture (CCC, nos. 109-114, 137).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. Read and interpret Sacred Scripture within the tradition and teaching of </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>the Church.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. Give attention both to what the human authors intended to say and to </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>what God reveals to us by their words.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Take into account the conditions of the time when it was written and the </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>culture where it was written.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>4. Read and interpret Sacred Scripture in the light of the same Holy Spirit by whom it was written (DV, nos. 12-13).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>5. Read and interpret each part of Sacred Scripture with an awareness </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>and understanding of the unity of the content and teaching of the entire </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Bible.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>6. Be attentive to the analogy of faith, that is, the unity that exists in all </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Church teaching.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>C. Senses of Scripture (CCC, nos. 115, 118-119).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. The literal sense: the meaning conveyed by the words of Scripture and discovered by exegesis (CCC, nos. 109-110, 116).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. The spiritual sense (CCC, no. 117).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>a. Allegorical sense: recognizing the significance of events in the </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Bible as they relate to Christ.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>b. Moral sense: Scripture teaches us and encourages us how to </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>live and act.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>c. Anagogical sense: Scripture speaks to us of eternal realities.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>D. The Bible in relation to science and history (CCC, nos. 37, 159, 1960).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. The Church teaches us how to relate truths of faith to science.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. There can be no conflict between religious truth and scientific and </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>historical truth (CCC, no. 159).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. The difference between the Catholic understanding of Scripture and </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>that of those who interpret the Bible in an overly literalist, fundamentalist way or with an approach limited to a symbolic understanding.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>VI. Challenges</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>C. Is the Bible always literally true?</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. It depends on what one means by “literally.” The Church does not </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>always propose a literalist or fundamentalist approach to Scripture but </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>rather a contextualist approach. The Church teaches that all of Scripture </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>is true on matters pertaining to religious and salvific teaching because it is </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>inspired by God for that purpose (CCC, nos. 107, 116).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. The Bible has a definite historic basis for events recounted in both the </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Old and the New Testaments; the Church particularly upholds the </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>historicity of the Gospels (CCC, no. 126). However, the Church does not </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>claim that the Bible’s purpose is to present scientific or historical facts </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>(CCC, no. 107).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. The Church gives guidelines for interpretation of Sacred Scripture.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. The Mission of Jesus Christ (The Paschal Mystery)</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>I. The Goodness of Creation and Our Fall from Grace</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>A. The Creation of the World and our first parents (CCC, nos. 54, 279-282).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. Revelation as found in the book of Genesis.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>a. Understanding literary forms in Scripture (CCC, no. 289).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>b. Genesis 1–11 conveys religious truth rather than science (CCC, </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>nos. 283-289).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>c. The book reveals truth about which science and history can only </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>speculate.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>d. Scripture’s use of figurative and symbolic language in Genesis </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1–11 (CCC, nos. 362, 375, 390, 396).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. The Trinitarian God is the Creator of all; all creation reflects the glory of </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>God (CCC, nos. 290-295, 301).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. God created all that is, seen and unseen.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>b. Seen or visible world (CCC, nos. 349-357).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>4. Human beings as the summit of creation.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Option A: Sacred Scripture</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>I. Divine Revelation: God Speaks to Us</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>A. God’s self-Revelation in words, deeds, covenants (CCC, nos. 50-53).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. Stages of Revelation (the history or divine plan of salvation) (CCC, nos. 54-55).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>C. Sacred Scripture (CCC, nos. 101-133).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. God is author—guarantees its truth about salvation (CCC, nos. 101-108).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. Word of God in words of man—literary forms—schools of biblical criticism or analysis.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Principles of interpretation (CCC, nos. 112-114).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>5. Senses of Scripture: literal; spiritual: allegorical, moral, anagogical (CCC, nos. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>115-119).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>6. Role of Scripture in the life of the Church (CCC, nos. 131-133).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>II. The Pentateuch or Torah—First Five Books of Scripture</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>A. Genesis, Exodus, Leviticus, Numbers, Deuteronomy.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. A major theory of the formation of these books is that they rely on several </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>sources—primarily four: Yahwist, Elohist, Priestly, Deuteronomic (J, E, P, D).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. Any and all parts of Scripture must be read and interpreted in relation to the </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Whole.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>B. Book of Genesis.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. Primeval history: 1–11—creation, Adam and Eve, the fall, promise of </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>redemption, and effects of sin told in figurative language (CCC, nos. 337, 362, </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>375; Compendium, nos. 51-78).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>2. Faith teachings in primeval history (NAB, Introduction).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Option B: History of the Catholic Church</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>II. History of Church in Post-Apostolic Times</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>9. The Age of Enlightenment</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>A. Rationalism, scientific model, Deism—Descartes, Voltaire, Rousseau.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>15. Vatican Council II: A Pastoral Approach to the World</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>D. Some developments after the Council.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>3. Developments in catechesis; understanding the need for both content and formation.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>Option E: Ecumenical and Interreligious Issues</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>I. Revelation and the Catholic Church</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>A. Tracing Divine Revelation through the history of salvation.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>1. Divine Revelation in the Old Testament times.</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>a. The Triune God is revealed in the work of Creation, which originates with the Father and is brought into being through the Word (Jesus Christ) by the power of the Holy Spirit (CCC, nos. 282, 314).</span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span><span><span>NGSS</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span><span><span><span><span><span>: </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>HS-LS4-1. Communicate scientific information that common ancestry and biological evolution are supported by multiple lines of empirical evidence. </span></span></span></span></span></span></p> <p> </p> <p><span><span><span><span><span><span>HS-LS4-2. Construct an explanation based on evidence that the process of evolution primarily results from four factors: (1) the potential for a species to increase in number, (2) the heritable genetic variation of individuals in a species due to mutation and sexual reproduction, (3) competition for limited resources, and (4) the proliferation of those organisms that are better able to survive and reproduce field--name-field-lesson-description field--type-string-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Short Description</h4> <div class="field__item">This lesson reflects upon the human reaction of wonder and awe to the created universe to inspire students to a deeper contemplation of scientific inquiry and study. Using Thomas Aquinas, Catholic scientists of major consequence, anatomy, and the concept of homeostasis, these dual science/theology lesson plans work in tandem to bridge the gap between faith and science. Ultimately students will be able to define awe and wonder and articulate the importance of awe and wonder as a starting point for both theological inquiry and scientific investigation. </div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge--lesson.html.twig * field--node--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig x field--node--lesson.html.twig * field--field-lesson-knowledge.html.twig * field--text-long.html.twig * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-knowledge field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Knowledge</h4> <div class="field__item"><p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>1.  Articulate the concept of Awe and Wonder </span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>2. Define homeostasis and the harmony of the body</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>3.  Compare and contrast scientific reasoning (scientific method) and theological reason</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><span><span><span><strong><span><span>4. Identify individuals who have reconciled faith and science.</span></span></strong></span></span></span></p> <p><br /> <br />  </p></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG --> <!-- THEME HOOK: 'field' --> <!-- FILE NAME SUGGESTIONS: * field.html.twig --> <!-- BEGIN OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <div class="field field--name-field-lesson-skills field--type-text-long field--label-above"> <h4 class="field__label">Skills</h4> <div class="field__item"><ul> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Explain the concept of awe and wonder </span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Research examples of scientific discoveries that has evoked a sense of awe and wonder</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> <li><span><span><span><strong><span><span>Synthesize the relationship of human body systems with the creative design that points to  God as anti-science</span></span></strong></span></span></span></li> </ul></div> </div> <!-- END OUTPUT from 'themes/custom/mcgrath/templates/lessons/field--node--lesson.html.twig' --> <!-- THEME DEBUG -->
